# DIFF gate — I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): agentic search as URL-DISCOVERY in the benchmark

DIFF gate. Review the committed code against the brief (`.codex/I-cap-002-agentic/brief.md`, brief-gate
APPROVE iter-2 in `codex_brief_verdict.txt`). Patch: `.codex/I-cap-002-agentic/codex_diff.patch` (branch
`bot/I-cap-002-agentic` on `bot/I-cap-002-depth`). **The #1 thing to red-team: the faithfulness contract —
can any agent summary/notebook field reach an evidence row?**

## What the diff does (5 files, +373)
1. **NEW `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/agentic_url_harvester.py`** (stdlib + `canonical_source_url`):
   - `harvest_agentic_urls(result, cap)` — ordered DETERMINISTIC union of `web_results` then
     `academic_results` `url` fields, then `agentic_url_accumulator`; dedup BY `canonical_source_url` but
     RETURNS the original fetchable URL; NEVER reads `agentic_research_notebook`/summaries/snippets;
     cap<=0 → []; robust to missing keys. (brief-gate iter-2 P2.1 canonical-key/original-value + P2.3
     deterministic ordered union.)
   - `merge_seed_url_evidence(staged_sources, staged_rows, new_sources, new_rows)` — pure dedup-by-`.url`
     source merge + only-accepted-source rows + global `ev_###` renumber from `len(staged_rows)`; copies
     inputs (no mutation); returns `(sources, rows, accepted_src, accepted_rows)`. (brief-gate iter-2 P2.2.)
2. **`run_honest_sweep_r3.py`** — agentic block AFTER the deepener (L~2505), BEFORE the retrieval-trace
   flush, flag-gated `PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK` default OFF:
   - Forces `searcher.PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED = False` (restored in `finally`) so the only LLM
     work is per-round analysis; books a conservative envelope (`PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS ×
     PG_AGENTIC_PER_ROUND_COST_USD`) into `_RUN_COST_CTX` and calls `check_run_budget(0)` BEFORE the try
     (so a `BudgetExceededError` PROPAGATES like STORM, not swallowed by the fail-open except).
   - Client built AFTER the precheck; `execute_agentic_search` run in an isolated `copy_context()` task;
     `harvest_agentic_urls(...)` then `del _ag_result` immediately; client + both flags restored in
     `finally`.
   - Discovered URLs fetched via `run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)`; `merge_seed_url_evidence`
     + `compute_tier_distribution`/`check_completeness`(gated on `not _use_research_planner`)/
     `assess_corpus_adequacy` recompute, then COMMIT to `retrieval`/`dist`/`completeness`/`adequacy`.
     Fail-open on the loop AND on the merge.
3. **`run_gate_b.py`** — `os.environ.setdefault("PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK", "1")`.
4. **Tests** — harvester (URLs-only; notebook IGNORED; canonical dedup keeps original; cap; malformed-safe)
   + merge (dup-URL rejection; renumber from staged base; no inflation; no input mutation) +
   activation test asserts the flag == "1".

## Red-team checklist — please confirm
- **Faithfulness:** trace every field consumed from the agentic result. Is it ONLY URLs? Can a notebook
  summary / snippet reach `direct_quote` or any evidence row? (The block harvests then `del`s the result.)
- **Budget airtight:** with `PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED=False`, is the per-round-analysis the only
  remaining LLM call path in `execute_agentic_search`? Does the envelope+precheck-before-try guarantee the
  cap can't be breached, and does `BudgetExceededError` correctly propagate (NOT caught by the agentic
  except)?
- **Atomic merge:** does `merge_seed_url_evidence` + the inline recompute-then-commit match the deepener's
  atomicity (a recompute error leaves the post-deepener corpus untouched)? Any id-collision / inflation
  path? (Evidence ids renumber from `len(staged_rows)`; only accepted-source rows are appended.)
- **Flag OFF → byte-unchanged:** with the flag unset, is the block fully skipped (corpus/manifest identical
  to feature-2 HEAD)?
- **Fail-open:** loop error, fetch error, AND merge error each leave the corpus untouched and let the run
  complete?
- **Scope/lifecycle:** are `_amplified_effective`, `compute_tier_distribution`, `check_completeness`,
  `assess_corpus_adequacy`, `protocol`, `_use_research_planner`, `retrieval` all in scope at the insertion
  point (the deepener directly above uses them)? Are the toggled module flags + client always restored/
  closed on every path?
- **LOC:** +373 (≈252 production: 130 sweep block + 116 harvester + 6 gate_b; 121 tests). This is one
  cohesive feature (harvester + wiring + activation are inseparable). Acceptable as a single PR (like the
  feature-2 depth PR at +344), or do you want it split (harvester module PR + wiring PR)?

@@ -0,0 +1,116 @@
+"""I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): harvest DISCOVERED URLs from an agentic-search result + a pure
+seed-URL evidence merge core.
+
+The agentic loop (``agents/searcher.execute_agentic_search``) is used in the benchmark for **URL
+DISCOVERY ONLY**. Its LLM-written page summaries (``agentic_research_notebook``) must NEVER become
+evidence — POLARIS's core invariant is verbatim-span faithfulness, and a model paraphrase masquerading
+as a ``direct_quote`` would be a fabrication. So we read ONLY the discovered URLs here; the discovered
+URLs are then fetched **verbatim** by ``live_retriever.run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)``
+and verified by strict_verify + the 4-role seam, exactly like the rest of the corpus.
+
+Two pure, stdlib-light functions (no network, no LLM, no new dependency):
+- ``harvest_agentic_urls`` — ordered, canonical-deduped, capped list of discovered URLs (originals).
+- ``merge_seed_url_evidence`` — the deepener's dedup-by-URL + global evidence-id renumber core, factored
+  out so it is unit-testable (and a future PR can repoint the deepener at it).
+"""
+
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+from typing import Any
+
+from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.saturation import canonical_source_url
+
+
+def harvest_agentic_urls(
+    agentic_result: dict[str, Any] | None,
+    cap: int = 200,
+) -> list[str]:
+    """Return ONLY the discovered URLs from an ``execute_agentic_search`` result.
+
+    Order-preserving and DETERMINISTIC: harvests from the ordered ``web_results`` then
+    ``academic_results`` streams first (these are the authoritative, complete, append-ordered streams —
+    incl. post-loop DDG / citation-chase URLs), then supplements with any ``agentic_url_accumulator``
+    entries not already seen. De-duplicates by ``canonical_source_url`` (scheme/tracking-stripped) but
+    RETURNS the original fetchable URL (canonical strings would hurt the live fetch yield). Returns at
+    most ``cap`` URLs. NEVER reads ``agentic_research_notebook`` / summaries / snippets. Robust to
+    missing/empty keys (returns ``[]`` rather than raising). ``cap <= 0`` → ``[]``.
+    """
+    if cap <= 0:
+        return []
+    result = agentic_result or {}
+    seen_canonical: set[str] = set()
+    out: list[str] = []
+
+    def _consider(raw: Any) -> None:
+        if len(out) >= cap:
+            return
+        url = (raw or "").strip() if isinstance(raw, str) else ""
+        if not url:
+            return
+        try:
+            key = canonical_source_url(url) or url
+        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — a malformed URL must not abort discovery
+            key = url
+        if key in seen_canonical:
+            return
+        seen_canonical.add(key)
+        out.append(url)
+
+    # Ordered result streams first (deterministic, complete).
+    for stream_key in ("web_results", "academic_results"):
+        for rec in result.get(stream_key, []) or []:
+            if len(out) >= cap:
+                return out
+            if isinstance(rec, dict):
+                _consider(rec.get("url"))
+    # Supplement with the accumulator (subset; set-ordered, so appended last for completeness only).
+    for url in result.get("agentic_url_accumulator", []) or []:
+        if len(out) >= cap:
+            return out
+        _consider(url)
+    return out
+
+
+def merge_seed_url_evidence(
+    staged_sources: list[Any],
+    staged_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
+    new_sources: list[Any],
+    new_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
+) -> tuple[list[Any], list[dict[str, Any]], int, int]:
+    """Dedup-by-URL source merge + global evidence-id renumber (the deepener's accepted-source core).
+
+    - ``new_sources`` whose ``.url`` is not already among ``staged_sources`` are appended; their URLs
+      form the ACCEPTED set.
+    - Only ``new_rows`` whose source URL (``source_url`` or ``url``) is in the ACCEPTED set are
+      appended — so a duplicate source contributes NO rows (no evidence_row_count inflation).
+    - Appended rows get a fresh ``evidence_id`` = ``ev_{base + i:03d}`` from ``len(staged_rows)`` so ids
+      never collide/overwrite.
+
+    Returns ``(merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_source_count, accepted_row_count)``. Operates on
+    COPIES; the inputs are not mutated. No I/O.
+    """
+    merged_sources = list(staged_sources)
+    seen_urls = {getattr(s, "url", None) for s in merged_sources}
+    accepted_src_urls: set[str] = set()
+    accepted_sources = 0
+    for src in new_sources:
+        url = getattr(src, "url", None)
+        if url and url not in seen_urls:
+            seen_urls.add(url)
+            merged_sources.append(src)
+            accepted_src_urls.add(url)
+            accepted_sources += 1
+
+    merged_rows = list(staged_rows)
+    base = len(merged_rows)
+    accepted_rows = 0
+    for ev in new_rows:
+        ev_url = (ev.get("source_url") or ev.get("url") or "").strip()
+        if not ev_url or ev_url not in accepted_src_urls:
+            continue  # duplicate / not an accepted source — skip (no inflation)
+        ev = dict(ev)  # copy so the caller's row object is not mutated
+        ev["evidence_id"] = f"ev_{base + accepted_rows:03d}"
+        merged_rows.append(ev)
+        accepted_rows += 1
+
+    return merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_sources, accepted_rows

+"""I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): tests for the agentic URL harvester + the pure seed-URL merge core.
+
+Faithfulness-critical: ``harvest_agentic_urls`` must read ONLY discovered URLs and NEVER the
+``agentic_research_notebook`` summaries. ``merge_seed_url_evidence`` must reject duplicate-URL sources
+and renumber evidence ids without inflation.
+"""
+
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+from dataclasses import dataclass
+
+from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.agentic_url_harvester import (
+    harvest_agentic_urls,
+    merge_seed_url_evidence,
+)
+
+
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+# harvest_agentic_urls
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+
+def test_harvests_ordered_union_of_web_then_academic():
+    result = {
+        "web_results": [{"url": "https://a.com/1"}, {"url": "https://b.com/2"}],
+        "academic_results": [{"url": "https://c.org/3"}],
+        "agentic_url_accumulator": ["https://d.net/4"],
+    }
+    out = harvest_agentic_urls(result)
+    assert out == [
+        "https://a.com/1",
+        "https://b.com/2",
+        "https://c.org/3",
+        "https://d.net/4",
+    ]
+
+
+def test_dedup_by_canonical_keeps_original_fetchable_url():
+    # http vs https of the same canonical resource -> one entry, the FIRST (original) URL is kept.
+    result = {
+        "web_results": [
+            {"url": "https://example.com/paper"},
+            {"url": "http://example.com/paper"},        # same canonical -> dropped
+        ],
+    }
+    out = harvest_agentic_urls(result)
+    assert out == ["https://example.com/paper"]
+    # the returned URL is the original (scheme intact), NOT the scheme-stripped canonical
+    assert out[0].startswith("https://")
+
+
+def test_notebook_and_summaries_are_never_read():
+    # A malicious/である result with a rich notebook + snippets must contribute NOTHING but the urls.
+    result = {
+        "web_results": [{"url": "https://real.com/x", "snippet": "model paraphrase"}],
+        "agentic_research_notebook": [
+            {"summary": "LLM-written paraphrase that must never be evidence", "url": "https://fake/note"},
+        ],
+    }
+    out = harvest_agentic_urls(result)
+    assert out == ["https://real.com/x"]            # notebook url NOT harvested, snippet ignored
+
+
+def test_cap_and_empty_and_malformed_are_safe():
+    assert harvest_agentic_urls(None) == []
+    assert harvest_agentic_urls({}) == []
+    assert harvest_agentic_urls({"web_results": []}) == []
+    assert harvest_agentic_urls({"web_results": [{"url": "https://a/1"}]}, cap=0) == []
+    # malformed records / missing url keys are skipped, not raised
+    safe = harvest_agentic_urls({"web_results": ["not a dict", {"no_url": 1}, {"url": ""}, {"url": "https://ok/1"}]})
+    assert safe == ["https://ok/1"]
+    capped = harvest_agentic_urls(
+        {"web_results": [{"url": f"https://h/{i}"} for i in range(50)]}, cap=10
+    )
+    assert len(capped) == 10
+    assert capped[0] == "https://h/0"
+
+
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+# merge_seed_url_evidence
+# --------------------------------------------------------------------------- #
+
+@dataclass
+class _Src:
+    url: str
+
+
+def test_merge_dedup_sources_and_renumber_rows():
+    staged_sources = [_Src("https://a/1")]
+    staged_rows = [{"evidence_id": "ev_000", "source_url": "https://a/1"}]
+    new_sources = [_Src("https://a/1"), _Src("https://b/2")]   # first is a duplicate
+    new_rows = [
+        {"source_url": "https://a/1", "direct_quote": "dup source row -> rejected"},
+        {"source_url": "https://b/2", "direct_quote": "new source row -> accepted"},
+    ]
+    sources, rows, acc_src, acc_rows = merge_seed_url_evidence(
+        staged_sources, staged_rows, new_sources, new_rows
+    )
+    assert acc_src == 1                              # only b/2 is a new source
+    assert acc_rows == 1                             # only the b/2 row is appended
+    assert [s.url for s in sources] == ["https://a/1", "https://b/2"]
+    # the new row was renumbered from the staged base (len==1 -> ev_001), no collision with ev_000
+    assert rows[-1]["evidence_id"] == "ev_001"
+    assert rows[-1]["source_url"] == "https://b/2"
+    assert len(rows) == 2                            # no inflation: the duplicate-source row was dropped
+
+
+def test_merge_does_not_mutate_inputs():
+    staged_sources = [_Src("https://a/1")]
+    staged_rows = [{"evidence_id": "ev_000", "source_url": "https://a/1"}]
+    new_rows = [{"source_url": "https://b/2", "direct_quote": "x"}]
+    merge_seed_url_evidence(staged_sources, staged_rows, [_Src("https://b/2")], new_rows)
+    assert len(staged_sources) == 1                  # caller's list untouched
+    assert len(staged_rows) == 1
+    assert "evidence_id" not in new_rows[0]          # caller's row dict not mutated

# Brief — I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): agentic search as URL-DISCOVERY in the benchmark path

## CHANGELOG vs iter 1 (your REQUEST_CHANGES, all addressed)
- **P1 (budget envelope not airtight w.r.t. content-reading/page-summary calls) — FIXED.** The benchmark
  agentic call now FORCES content reading OFF by toggling the import-cached module constant
  `searcher.PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED = False` for the call (restored in `finally`, exactly the
  STORM `PG_STORM_ENABLED` toggle pattern). Confirmed: `searcher.py` imports it as a module constant (L73)
  and the page-summary block reads it as the module global (`if PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED:` L1766).
  With it OFF, the ONLY LLM work in the loop is `_agentic_round_analysis` (≤ `PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS` calls),
  so the envelope `PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS × PG_AGENTIC_PER_ROUND_COST_USD` covers ALL bounded LLM work — the
  cap is airtight. Belt-and-suspenders: the loop runs in an isolated `copy_context()` and its real spend is
  discarded from the parent total (the envelope IS the parent's accounting), so even an unexpected call
  cannot breach `PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN`. See §4.3 step 2.
- **P2 (discard the agentic result right after harvest) — FIXED.** Only `_urls = harvest_agentic_urls(...)`
  survives; the full result dict is `del`'d immediately so no notebook/summary field exists in scope near
  the merge. See §4.3 step 3.
- **P2 (merge dedup/renumber tests) — FIXED.** The dedup-by-URL + global evidence-id renumber core is
  extracted into a PURE helper `merge_seed_url_evidence(...)` in the harvester module and unit-tested for
  duplicate-URL rejection + id-renumber + no-inflation. See §4.2 + §8.

## 0. What this gate reviews
BRIEF gate (design correctness). Code does not exist yet. The single most important thing to red-team here
is the **faithfulness contract** (§4.1): the agentic loop must only DISCOVER URLs; agent-written summaries
must NEVER become evidence. Confirm the design cannot launder a summary into a `direct_quote`.

## 1. Context
Operator: "B then A". Wire the four Tier-B capabilities into the **benchmark (Pipeline A)**, then run the
1000-URL beat-both. POLARIS has TWO pipelines: A = benchmark (`run_gate_b` →
`run_honest_sweep_r3.run_one_query` → `live_retriever` → 4-role seam); B = web-UI LangGraph (`graph.py` +
`agents/`). The agentic loop (`agents/searcher.execute_agentic_search`) is consumed only by Pipeline B; it is
a NO-OP for the benchmark. Feature 1/4 STORM (PR #1061) and feature 2/4 depth-gate (PR #1062) are DONE
(Codex-approved). This is **feature 3/4 — the largest, highest-risk one**.

## 2. The capability today (Pipeline B only) + the faithfulness hazard
`execute_agentic_search(state, client)` (searcher.py L1591) runs a multi-round seed→search→reason loop:
each round generates follow-up queries from prior results, optionally READS page content into a
`research_notebook` of LLM **summaries** (`PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED`,
`PG_AGENTIC_SUMMARY_MAX_TOKENS`), and converges on saturation/budget. It returns (L1885):
```
{ "web_results": [...], "academic_results": [...], "agentic_url_accumulator": [<=500 deduped urls],
  "agentic_research_notebook": [<summaries>], "agentic_search_rounds", "agentic_knowledge_gaps", ... }
```
**THE HAZARD:** `agentic_research_notebook` is LLM-written page summaries. POLARIS's core invariant is
verbatim-span faithfulness — every delivered sentence cites a `[#ev:id:start-end]` span that strict_verify
checks against fetched source text. If a notebook summary were turned into an evidence row's `direct_quote`,
it would be a model paraphrase masquerading as a source span — a fabrication that defeats the whole product.
So the benchmark wiring uses the agentic loop for **URL DISCOVERY ONLY**.

## 3. Goal of feature 3/4
Behind a default-OFF flag (Gate-B activates it), run the agentic loop to DISCOVER additional high-quality
URLs, then fetch those URLs **verbatim** through the SAME `run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)`
chokepoint that the rest of the corpus goes through — so every discovered source earns its tier only from
fetched content and is strict_verify'd + 4-role-checked identically. The agentic notebook/summaries are
discarded. This directly serves the "search up to 1000 high-quality URLs" depth target by widening
discovery beyond the static Serper/S2 fan-out, without touching faithfulness.

## 4. Design (what the diff will implement)

### 4.1 Faithfulness contract (the core invariant — please verify this is airtight)
- The ONLY thing consumed from the agentic result is **URLs** (`agentic_url_accumulator`, plus the `url`
  field of `web_results`/`academic_results` as a fallback union). `agentic_research_notebook`,
  `agentic_knowledge_gaps`, and every summary/snippet field are IGNORED — never read, never written to any
  evidence row.
- Discovered URLs are fetched via `run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=urls, seed_only=True, …)` — the SAME
  fetch/tier/strict_verify path the deepener already uses (L2406-2468). A thin/abstract-only/denied page is
  DROPPED fail-closed exactly as today; no laundering.
- The merged evidence rows are the verbatim-fetched `direct_quote`s produced by `live_retriever`, identical
  in kind to the primary-retrieval rows. The 4-role seam + strict_verify run on them unchanged.

### 4.2 New harvester + merge module
`src/polaris_graph/retrieval/agentic_url_harvester.py` (stdlib + the existing `canonical_source_url`
helper; no network, no LLM, no new dependency):
```python
def harvest_agentic_urls(agentic_result: dict | None, cap: int = 200) -> list[str]:
    """Return ONLY discovered URLs from an execute_agentic_search() result — order-preserving,
    deduped (canonical_source_url), capped. Prefers 'agentic_url_accumulator'; falls back to the 'url'
    field of web_results+academic_results. NEVER reads agentic_research_notebook / summaries / snippets.
    cap<=0 -> []. Robust to missing keys."""

def merge_seed_url_evidence(staged_sources, staged_rows, new_sources, new_rows):
    """PURE merge core (P2.2): dedup new_sources by URL against staged_sources, append only accepted
    non-duplicate sources, and append only new_rows whose source URL was an ACCEPTED non-duplicate
    source — with a GLOBAL ev_### renumber from len(staged_rows) so ids never collide/inflate. Returns
    (merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_source_count, accepted_row_count). No I/O. This is the
    deepener's accepted-source/renumber logic factored out so it is unit-testable (and a future PR can
    point the deepener at it too — noted as follow-up, not done here to keep blast radius small)."""
```
Both unit-tested. The benchmark block calls `merge_seed_url_evidence` for the source/row staging, then
recomputes `compute_tier_distribution` + completeness/adequacy over the staged corpus and commits on success
(the recompute stays inline because it closes over run-local objects).

### 4.3 Wire into `run_one_query` — mirror the deepener (the proven pattern)
Placed AFTER the primary retrieval (L2129) and AFTER the existing deepener block (so it is an additional,
independent URL source), behind `PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK` (default OFF), reusing the **exact
STORM-style budget + isolation pattern** I already shipped (L2003-2070) and the **exact deepener atomic-merge
pattern** (L2445-2500+):
1. Build a minimal `ResearchState` the loop needs: `original_query`, `region`, `sub_queries`
   (the amplified/effective queries), `web_results: []`, `academic_results: []`.
2. **Force content reading OFF + airtight budget (P1 fix):** set `searcher.PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED
   = False` for the call (toggle the import-cached module constant, restore the prior value in `finally`,
   STORM pattern) — the benchmark discards the notebook anyway, so paying for page summaries is pure waste,
   AND it removes the only un-enveloped LLM term. The remaining LLM work is `_agentic_round_analysis`
   (≤ `PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS` calls), so BOOK a CONSERVATIVE envelope
   (`PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS × PG_AGENTIC_PER_ROUND_COST_USD`, env-tunable) into `_RUN_COST_CTX` and ENFORCE
   the cap (`check_run_budget(0)`) BEFORE running; construct the client AFTER the precheck; run the loop in
   an isolated `copy_context()` task (real spend discarded from the parent — the envelope IS the parent's
   accounting); close the client in `finally`. Over-books, never under-enforces (LAW VI).
3. `_urls = harvest_agentic_urls(result, cap=PG_AGENTIC_BENCHMARK_URL_CAP)`; then `del result` immediately so
   no notebook/summary field is in scope near the merge (P2.1). Only `_urls` (a `list[str]`) survives.
4. If `_urls`: `agentic_retrieval = run_live_retrieval(research_question=q["question"], amplified_queries=[],
   protocol=protocol, fetch_cap=min(len(_urls), cap), enable_openalex_enrich=True,
   enable_prefetch_filter=False, seed_urls=_urls, seed_only=True)`.
5. **ATOMIC merge mirroring the deepener, via the pure helper:** call `merge_seed_url_evidence(...)` (§4.2)
   to stage deduped sources + renumbered rows, recompute `compute_tier_distribution` + completeness/adequacy
   over the staged corpus, and COMMIT to `retrieval`/`evidence_for_gen` only after every recompute succeeds.
   Any error → fail-open, post-primary corpus untouched.
6. Broad `except` logs `[agentic] … failed — proceeding without agentic URLs` and continues.

### 4.4 Gate-B activation (mirrors STORM/quantified/V30)
`run_gate_b_query`: `os.environ.setdefault("PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK", "1")` so the paid benchmark
runs agentic discovery; `setdefault` keeps the operator override (LAW VI).

### 4.5 Invariants the diff MUST hold
1. **URL-discovery only** — no summary/notebook/snippet ever becomes an evidence row or `direct_quote`; the
   result dict is discarded right after URL harvest (only a `list[str]` survives).
2. **Same verify chokepoint** — discovered URLs go through `run_live_retrieval(seed_only=True)` +
   strict_verify + 4-role, identical to the deepener; thin/denied pages dropped fail-closed.
3. **Budget cap airtight** — content reading forced OFF (only `_agentic_round_analysis` LLM calls remain),
   conservative envelope booked + enforced BEFORE the loop, isolated context discards real spend; agentic
   LLM spend can never breach `PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN`.
4. **Flag default OFF → byte-unchanged** legacy honest-sweep; Gate-B turns it ON.
5. **Fail-open** — any agentic/fetch/merge error leaves the primary corpus untouched; the run completes.
6. **Atomic merge** — pure-helper staging + recompute-then-commit, so a partial merge can't corrupt the
   corpus (deepener Codex-approved pattern).
7. **Client + flag lifecycle** — client built after the budget precheck, closed in `finally`;
   `PG_AGENTIC_CONTENT_READING_ENABLED` restored in `finally`.

## 5. Files I have ALSO checked
- `agents/searcher.py:1591` `execute_agentic_search` — return shape confirmed (L1885): `web_results`,
  `academic_results`, `agentic_url_accumulator` (clean deduped urls), `agentic_research_notebook`
  (summaries — IGNORED). Reads `state["original_query"|"region"|"sub_queries"]`.
- `retrieval/live_retriever.py:2158` `run_live_retrieval(..., seed_urls=…, seed_only=…)` — the verbatim
  seed-fetch path the deepener uses.
- `run_honest_sweep_r3.py` deepener L2406-2468 (URL-discovery → seed_only fetch → atomic staged merge →
  fail-open) is the merge template; gap-search L3139-3180 is the query-merge variant (not used here).
- STORM block L2003-2070 — the budget-envelope + isolated-context + fail-open + client-close template I reuse.
- `agents/planner.py` `PG_AGENTIC_SEED_QUERIES`; `state.py` agentic flags (MAX_ROUNDS/MAX_QUERIES/
  MAX_TIME_SECONDS/…) already exist and bound the loop internally.

## 6. Resolved design decisions (iter-1 open questions, now closed)
- **Merge reuse:** the dedup-by-URL + evidence-id-renumber CORE is now a pure tested helper
  `merge_seed_url_evidence` (shared-ready); the completeness/adequacy recompute stays inline (it closes over
  run-local objects). Deepener is NOT touched in this PR (a follow-up can repoint it). Low blast radius.
- **Placement:** AFTER the deepener — an independent additional URL source. (The deepener is borderline-gated
  and S2-only; agentic is a broader web/academic discoverer; keeping them separate fetches is clearer and
  each fails open independently.)
- **Content reading + budget:** RESOLVED — content reading is FORCED OFF for the benchmark agentic call, so
  the envelope `PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS × PG_AGENTIC_PER_ROUND_COST_USD` covers all remaining LLM work; the cap
  is airtight (§4.3 step 2). No remaining open questions.

## 7. Acceptance (GREEN)
- New `agentic_url_harvester.py` (URLs-only, never touches notebook) + unit tests.
- `run_one_query` agentic block: flag-gated default OFF, budget-enveloped, isolated-context, fetch via
  `seed_only=True`, atomic merge mirroring the deepener, fail-open. Flag OFF → manifest/corpus byte-unchanged.
- `run_gate_b_query` activates `PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK`; activation test asserts it == "1".
- No summary/notebook content can become evidence (test the harvester ignores notebook).
- ≤ ~200 LOC of net production change (mirror-merge may push this; flag if so).

## 8. Smoke plan (offline)
1. `pytest` the harvester unit tests: `harvest_agentic_urls` (URLs-only; notebook IGNORED even when present;
   cap; canonical dedup; missing-keys safe) + `merge_seed_url_evidence` (duplicate-URL rejection; only
   accepted-source rows appended; global ev_### renumber from the staged base; no row inflation).
2. Extend + run the benchmark-stack activation test (asserts `PG_AGENTIC_SEARCH_IN_BENCHMARK` == "1").
3. `py_compile` the touched files; import-smoke `searcher` + the harvester.
4. (Live agentic discovery needs network + spend — that is the Tier-A VM run, not this offline gate.)

 succeeded in 1747ms:
"""I-cap-002 feature 3/4 (#1060): harvest DISCOVERED URLs from an agentic-search result + a pure
seed-URL evidence merge core.

The agentic loop (``agents/searcher.execute_agentic_search``) is used in the benchmark for **URL
DISCOVERY ONLY**. Its LLM-written page summaries (``agentic_research_notebook``) must NEVER become
evidence — POLARIS's core invariant is verbatim-span faithfulness, and a model paraphrase masquerading
as a ``direct_quote`` would be a fabrication. So we read ONLY the discovered URLs here; the discovered
URLs are then fetched **verbatim** by ``live_retriever.run_live_retrieval(seed_urls=…, seed_only=True)``
and verified by strict_verify + the 4-role seam, exactly like the rest of the corpus.

Two pure, stdlib-light functions (no network, no LLM, no new dependency):
- ``harvest_agentic_urls`` — ordered, canonical-deduped, capped list of discovered URLs (originals).
- ``merge_seed_url_evidence`` — the deepener's dedup-by-URL + global evidence-id renumber core, factored
  out so it is unit-testable (and a future PR can repoint the deepener at it).
"""

from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Any

from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.saturation import canonical_source_url


def harvest_agentic_urls(
    agentic_result: dict[str, Any] | None,
    cap: int = 200,
) -> list[str]:
    """Return ONLY the discovered URLs from an ``execute_agentic_search`` result.

    Order-preserving and DETERMINISTIC: harvests from the ordered ``web_results`` then
    ``academic_results`` streams first (these are the authoritative, complete, append-ordered streams —
    incl. post-loop DDG / citation-chase URLs), then supplements with any ``agentic_url_accumulator``
    entries not already seen. De-duplicates by ``canonical_source_url`` (scheme/tracking-stripped) but
    RETURNS the original fetchable URL (canonical strings would hurt the live fetch yield). Returns at
    most ``cap`` URLs. NEVER reads ``agentic_research_notebook`` / summaries / snippets. Robust to
    missing/empty keys (returns ``[]`` rather than raising). ``cap <= 0`` → ``[]``.
    """
    if cap <= 0:
        return []
    result = agentic_result or {}
    seen_canonical: set[str] = set()
    out: list[str] = []

    def _consider(raw: Any) -> None:
        if len(out) >= cap:
            return
        url = (raw or "").strip() if isinstance(raw, str) else ""
        if not url:
            return
        try:
            key = canonical_source_url(url) or url
        except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — a malformed URL must not abort discovery
            key = url
        if key in seen_canonical:
            return
        seen_canonical.add(key)
        out.append(url)

    # Ordered result streams first (deterministic, complete).
    for stream_key in ("web_results", "academic_results"):
        for rec in result.get(stream_key, []) or []:
            if len(out) >= cap:
                return out
            if isinstance(rec, dict):
                _consider(rec.get("url"))
    # Supplement with the accumulator (subset; set-ordered, so appended last for completeness only).
    for url in result.get("agentic_url_accumulator", []) or []:
        if len(out) >= cap:
            return out
        _consider(url)
    return out


def merge_seed_url_evidence(
    staged_sources: list[Any],
    staged_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
    new_sources: list[Any],
    new_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
) -> tuple[list[Any], list[dict[str, Any]], int, int]:
    """Dedup-by-URL source merge + global evidence-id renumber (the deepener's accepted-source core).

    - ``new_sources`` whose ``.url`` is not already among ``staged_sources`` are appended; their URLs
      form the ACCEPTED set.
    - Only ``new_rows`` whose source URL (``source_url`` or ``url``) is in the ACCEPTED set are
      appended — so a duplicate source contributes NO rows (no evidence_row_count inflation).
    - Appended rows get a fresh ``evidence_id`` = ``ev_{base + i:03d}`` from ``len(staged_rows)`` so ids
      never collide/overwrite.

    Returns ``(merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_source_count, accepted_row_count)``. Operates on
    COPIES; the inputs are not mutated. No I/O.
    """
    merged_sources = list(staged_sources)
    seen_urls = {getattr(s, "url", None) for s in merged_sources}
    accepted_src_urls: set[str] = set()
    accepted_sources = 0
    for src in new_sources:
        url = getattr(src, "url", None)
        if url and url not in seen_urls:
            seen_urls.add(url)
            merged_sources.append(src)
            accepted_src_urls.add(url)
            accepted_sources += 1

    merged_rows = list(staged_rows)
    base = len(merged_rows)
    accepted_rows = 0
    for ev in new_rows:
        ev_url = (ev.get("source_url") or ev.get("url") or "").strip()
        if not ev_url or ev_url not in accepted_src_urls:
            continue  # duplicate / not an accepted source — skip (no inflation)
        ev = dict(ev)  # copy so the caller's row object is not mutated
        ev["evidence_id"] = f"ev_{base + accepted_rows:03d}"
        merged_rows.append(ev)
        accepted_rows += 1

    return merged_sources, merged_rows, accepted_sources, accepted_rows

01591: async def execute_agentic_search(
01592:     state: ResearchState,
01593:     client,
01594: ) -> dict:
01595:     """Execute searches via an agentic loop: seed -> search -> reason -> repeat.
01596: 
01597:     Each round generates targeted follow-up queries informed by prior results.
01598:     Converges when multiple signals indicate saturation or budget is exhausted.
01599: 
01600:     Returns state update compatible with the existing graph contract:
01601:     web_results, academic_results, status, plus agentic metadata.
01602:     """
01603:     web_search_fn, academic_search_fn = _import_search_tools()

01605:     original_query = state["original_query"]

01610:     seen_urls: set[str] = set()
01611:     round_summaries: list[dict] = []
01612:     perspective_hits: dict[str, int] = {p: 0 for p in STORM_PERSPECTIVES}
01613:     total_queries = 0

01618:     consecutive_empty_rounds = 0  # FIX: Track empty rounds to prevent degenerate loops
01619: 
01620:     tracer = get_tracer()
01621: 
01622:     for round_num in range(1, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_ROUNDS + 1):
01623:         # Budget checks

01625:         if elapsed > PG_AGENTIC_MAX_TIME_SECONDS:
01626:             logger.info(
01627:                 "[polaris graph] Agentic loop: time budget exhausted "
01628:                 "(%.0fs > %ds) after %d rounds",
01629:                 elapsed, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_TIME_SECONDS, round_num - 1,
01630:             )
01631:             break
01632:         if total_queries >= PG_AGENTIC_MAX_QUERIES:
01633:             logger.info(
01634:                 "[polaris graph] Agentic loop: query budget exhausted "

01636:                 total_queries, PG_AGENTIC_MAX_QUERIES, round_num - 1,
01637:             )
01638:             break

01642:             web_q, acad_q, exa_q = _partition_seeds(sub_queries)

01645:             try:

01651:                         round_summaries=round_summaries,

01653:                         round_number=round_num,

01657:                 )
01658:             except asyncio.TimeoutError:

00227: def reset_run_cost() -> None:
00228:     """Reset the current task's run-cost accumulator to 0. Call at the
00229:     start of a run. Uses ContextVar so concurrent async tasks each get
00230:     their own zero-start."""
00231:     _RUN_COST_CTX.set(0.0)

00234: def current_run_cost() -> float:
00235:     """Return the cumulative cost of the current run (USD), scoped to
00236:     the current asyncio task via ContextVar."""
00237:     return _RUN_COST_CTX.get()

00240: def _add_run_cost(delta: float) -> None:
00241:     # BUG-B-201: ContextVar-scoped cost accumulator. Each async task has
00242:     # its own run-cost; concurrent gather() of run_one_query() no longer
00243:     # stomps each other.
00244:     _RUN_COST_CTX.set(_RUN_COST_CTX.get() + float(delta))
00245: 
00246: 
00247: # Codex round 1 B-4: conservative per-model prices used when OpenRouter
00248: # omits usage.cost. Prices are $/M tokens and represent the UPPER END of
00249: # published rates for each provider family (if a cheaper provider is used
00250: # we overcharge the run cost, which is the safe direction for a budget
00251: # guard). When the model is unknown we use OPUS-tier defaults.
00252: _PRICE_TABLE_USD_PER_M: dict[str, tuple[float, float]] = {
00253:     # model prefix  :  (input $/M, output $/M)
00254:     # IMPORTANT: longer/more-specific prefixes first. Dict insertion order
00255:     # = iteration order = first-match-wins per _impute_cost_from_tokens.
00256:     # I-cd-010 / GH#625: qwen/qwen3-8b + z-ai/glm-5.1 entries are
00257:     # INTENTIONAL pricing-table coverage for env-overridden models (set
00258:     # PG_GENERATOR_MODEL / OPENROUTER_DEFAULT_MODEL); not the active
00259:     # Carney demo lock defaults.
00260:     "deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro":   (0.435, 0.87),
00261:     "deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash": (0.14, 0.28),
00262:     "deepseek/":       (0.27, 0.38),
00263:     "qwen/qwen3-8b":   (0.05, 0.40),
00264:     "qwen/qwen3-32b":  (0.10, 0.60),
00265:     "qwen/":           (0.10, 0.60),
00266:     "z-ai/glm-5.1":    (0.60, 2.20),
00267:     "z-ai/":           (0.60, 2.20),
00268:     # I-run11-004: MiniMax-M2 Sentinel (decomposition). Conservative upper-bound $/M so the
00269:     # budget-impute fallback never UNDERcharges (over-counting is the safe direction for the cap).
00270:     "minimax/minimax-m2": (0.55, 2.20),
00271:     "minimax/":           (0.55, 2.20),
00272:     "meta-llama/":     (0.30, 0.90),
00273:     "google/gemma-4-31b-it": (0.13, 0.38),
00274:     "google/gemma":    (0.05, 0.30),
00275:     "google/gemini":   (1.25, 5.00),
00276:     "mistralai/":      (0.30, 0.90),
00277:     "moonshotai/":     (0.60, 2.50),
00278:     "openai/":         (3.00, 10.00),
00279:     "anthropic/":      (3.00, 15.00),
00280: }
00281: 
00282: _DEFAULT_PRICE_PER_M = (3.00, 15.00)  # Opus-tier worst-case
00283: 
00284: 
00285: def _impute_cost_from_tokens(
00286:     model: str,
00287:     input_tokens: int,
00288:     output_tokens: int,
00289:     reasoning_tokens: int,
00290: ) -> float:
00291:     """Estimate $/call from token counts + published prices. Reasoning
00292:     tokens bill at the output rate (matches OpenAI / Anthropic practice).
00293:     Used by the budget guard when OpenRouter omits usage.cost.
00294: 
00295:     Defensive: token counts are clamped to >=0. A corrupted API response
00296:     returning negative tokens must NOT produce a negative cost that
00297:     would silently shrink the accumulated run budget and let a runaway
00298:     loop keep calling past PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN.
00299:     """
00300:     # Clamp negative token counts — these can only come from a
00301:     # corrupted API response. A negative cost here would be silently
00302:     # absorbed by _add_run_cost and weaken the budget guard.
00303:     input_tokens = max(0, int(input_tokens))
00304:     output_tokens = max(0, int(output_tokens))
00305:     reasoning_tokens = max(0, int(reasoning_tokens))
00306:     if input_tokens == 0 and output_tokens == 0 and reasoning_tokens == 0:
00307:         return 0.0
00308:     model_lower = (model or "").lower()
00309:     input_rate, output_rate = _DEFAULT_PRICE_PER_M
00310:     for prefix, (in_r, out_r) in _PRICE_TABLE_USD_PER_M.items():
00311:         if model_lower.startswith(prefix):
00312:             input_rate, output_rate = in_r, out_r
00313:             break
00314:     return (
00315:         (input_tokens / 1_000_000.0) * input_rate
00316:         + ((output_tokens + reasoning_tokens) / 1_000_000.0) * output_rate
00317:     )
00318: 
00319: 
00320: def check_run_budget(anticipated_additional: float = 0.0) -> None:
00321:     """Raise BudgetExceededError if the next call would exceed the cap.
00322: 
00323:     anticipated_additional: optional estimate of the upcoming call cost
00324:     (used only for guard-before-call — the actual cost is recorded by
00325:     `_add_run_cost()` after the call returns).
00326:     """
00327:     current = current_run_cost()
00328:     projected = current + max(0.0, float(anticipated_additional))
00329:     if projected > PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN:
00330:         raise BudgetExceededError(
00331:             f"PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN={PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN:.4f} exceeded: "
00332:             f"current=${current:.4f} + anticipated=${anticipated_additional:.4f} "
00333:             f"= ${projected:.4f}. Set PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN higher or call "
00334:             f"reset_run_cost() between runs."
00335:         )

02530:     async def generate_structured(
02531:         self,
02532:         prompt: str,
02533:         schema: Type[T],
02534:         system: str = "",
02535:         max_tokens: int = 8192,
02536:         timeout: Optional[float] = None,
02537:         reasoning_enabled: bool = False,
02538:         reasoning_effort: str = "high",
02539:         reasoning_max_tokens: Optional[int] = None,
02540:         reasoning_exclude: Optional[bool] = None,
02541:     ) -> T:
02542:         """
02543:         Structured output call — reasoning OFF by default, returns parsed schema.
02544: 
02545:         When reasoning is DISABLED and PG_STRICT_JSON_SCHEMA=1 (default),
02546:         sends response_format with json_schema + strict:true to enforce
02547:         schema compliance at the provider level (Qwen 3.5 Plus supports this).
02548: 
02549:         When reasoning is ENABLED, relies on prompt-based JSON extraction
02550:         because thinking + json_schema response_format are incompatible.
02551: 
02552:         FIX-QM1: When reasoning IS explicitly enabled, checks both content
02553:         and reasoning_content for JSON (some models put JSON in reasoning).
02554:         """
02555:         # Use strict:true JSON schema when reasoning is disabled and env allows.
02556:         # Qwen3.5-Plus supports strict schema enforcement. Gate behind
02557:         # PG_STRICT_JSON_SCHEMA (default "1") for backwards compatibility.
02558:         # When reasoning is enabled, skip — thinking + json_schema are incompatible.

tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:1:Building on the clinical rationale for non-pharmacological glycemic strategies, this section examines how intermittent fasting (IF) modifies the metabolic pathways most relevant to type 2 diabetes mellitus (T2DM), drawing on weighted and standardized mean differences from systematic reviews that aggregate over 50 clinical studies comparing IF protocols against caloric restriction and usual-diet controls [CITE:ev_12e3ca8d07d9d3ed].
tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:5:Weight reduction is the most consistently observed outcome across IF trials, and it is mechanistically central to the improvement of insulin resistance in T2DM. In adults with overweight or obesity, IF reduced fat mass by a mean difference of −0.72 kg compared with a non-intervention diet [CITE:ev_243de27dc515c169]. When IF is combined with structured physical exercise, the weight reduction relative to a control diet plus exercise reaches a weighted mean difference of −1.83 kg (P = 0.001) [CITE:ev_749f00cb5c5eea28], suggesting an additive effect when caloric timing is paired with energy expenditure. The largest effect size is observed with modified alternate-day fasting, which produced a weight reduction of −5.18 kg (95% CI: −7.04 to −3.32) compared with a usual diet, supported by high certainty of evidence [CITE:ev_e7bdb4797d3f6f0f]. The differential between these protocols is clinically meaningful: a five-kilogram loss falls within the range associated with measurable improvements in HbA1c and insulin sensitivity, whereas sub-kilogram fat-mass reductions, although statistically significant, may yield more modest glycemic benefits.
tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:7:The pattern of fat redistribution is equally important. Beyond aggregate weight loss, IF is associated with a modification of the distribution of abdominal fat in people with obesity and T2DM, alongside improvements in glycemic control [CITE:ev_dde1177bb61ef9e9]. Because visceral adiposity is a stronger predictor of hepatic insulin resistance than total body weight, the redistribution pattern offers a plausible mechanistic bridge between fasting-induced energy deficits and downstream glycemic improvements relevant to T2DM management.
tests\fixtures\subagent_prompts\section_writer_response.txt:11:The lipid response to IF reinforces its cardiometabolic relevance for the T2DM population, where dyslipidemia is a frequent comorbidity. Across umbrella-review syntheses, IF reduced low-density lipoprotein cholesterol by a standardized mean difference of −0.20 (95% CI: −0.38 to −0.02; p = 0.027) compared with a non-intervention diet [CITE:ev_410655e66705beb6]. When IF is combined with exercise, the reduction is larger and reported in absolute units: a weighted mean difference of −5.35 mg/dL (P = 0.03) for LDL cholesterol [CITE:ev_39b4891376876856]. Triacylglycerols also fall under IF protocols, with a standardized mean difference of −0.23 (95% CI: −0.39 to −0.06; p = 0.007) [CITE:ev_e273c28dab55ecd8]. The convergence of LDL and triglyceride reductions is consistent with the broader observation that IF exerts beneficial effects on the lipid profile [CITE:ev_dde1177bb61ef9e9], a finding that strengthens its candidacy as an adjunctive intervention for individuals with T2DM whose treatment goals extend beyond glycemic control to encompass cardiovascular risk attenuation.

02158: def run_live_retrieval(
02159:     *,
02160:     research_question: str,
02161:     amplified_queries: Optional[list[str]] = None,
02162:     protocol: Optional[dict[str, Any]] = None,
02163:     max_serper: int = DEFAULT_MAX_SERPER,
02164:     max_s2: int = DEFAULT_MAX_S2,
02165:     fetch_cap: int = DEFAULT_FETCH_CAP,
02166:     enable_openalex_enrich: bool = True,
02167:     enable_prefetch_filter: bool = False,
02168:     domain: Optional[str] = None,
02169:     seed_urls: Optional[list[str]] = None,
02170:     seed_only: bool = False,
02171:     research_frame: Any = None,
02172:     anchor_seed: bool = True,
02173: ) -> LiveRetrievalResult:
02174:     """Execute live retrieval and classify the corpus.
02175: 
02176:     Args:
02177:         research_question: Raw user query (anchor for scope validator).
02178:         amplified_queries: Optional extra queries (scope-validated).
02179:         protocol: Protocol dict; used for scope validation.
02180:         max_serper: Max Serper results per query.
02181:         max_s2: Max S2 results per query.
02182:         fetch_cap: Hard cap on total URLs to fetch (cost control).
02183:         enable_openalex_enrich: Toggle OpenAlex lookup per URL.
02184:         enable_prefetch_filter: Toggle embedding-based off-topic filter
02185:             (slow; off by default for the first live run).
02186:         domain: Optional scope-template domain name (clinical / policy /
02187:             tech / due_diligence). When set, R-6 Gap-2 domain backends
02188:             augment the generic Serper+S2 retrieval with arxiv (tech),
02189:             SEC EDGAR (DD), or policy-site targeted Serper queries.
02190:         research_frame: Optional planner `ResearchFrame` (I-meta-005 Phase 2
02191:             #986). When set (ON-mode), the field-agnostic need-type registry
02192:             REPLACES the domain backends at the Step-2a seam — discovery is
02193:             keyed on the frame's declared `evidence_needs` + extracted
02194:             `jurisdictions`, NOT a domain. Mutually exclusive with `domain` on
02195:             the on-path (the sweep passes `domain=None` on-mode).
02196:         anchor_seed: When True (default — OFF-mode byte-identical), the verbatim
02197:             `research_question` is PREPENDED to the effective query list and the
02198:             scope validator keeps it (`always_keep_anchor=True`). I-meta-005
02199:             Phase 4 (#988) GAP rounds pass `anchor_seed=False` so the broad anchor
02200:             is NOT re-fired: `all_queries = amplified_queries` ONLY, the scope
02201:             validator does NOT re-add the anchor (`always_keep_anchor=False`), and
02202:             the need-type backend is invoked with `anchor_seed=False` (no
02203:             `research_question` prepend there either). A gap round therefore fires
02204:             EXACTLY the gap sub-queries on BOTH the core Serper/S2 seam AND the
02205:             need-type adapters.

02208:

02210:         MalformedPlanError: when `research_frame` carries a malformed
02211:             `evidence_needs` value OR a malformed jurisdiction SHAPE. This is
02212:             validated UP-FRONT (before ANY live discovery, incl. core
02213:             Serper/S2) and FAILS LOUD — it NEVER silently degrades to core
02214:             Serper/S2 (brief §2.4 P2-note-1). Distinct from the fail-OPEN
02215:             adapter/network handling at the Step-2a seam.
02216:     """

02218:     notes: list[str] = []
02219: 
02220:     # ── Step 0: UP-FRONT plan validation (I-meta-005 Phase 2, P2-note-1) ──
02221:     # A malformed frame (bad evidence_need / bad jurisdiction SHAPE) must FAIL
02222:     # LOUD here — BEFORE the core Serper/S2 baseline spends or populates any
02223:     # candidate. The router's validation raises MalformedPlanError; we let it
02224:     # propagate (it is a VALIDATION error, distinct from the fail-OPEN
02225:     # adapter/network handling at Step 2a). Only fires on-mode (frame present).
02226:     if research_frame is not None and not seed_only:
02227:         from src.polaris_graph.discovery.need_type_router import (
02228:             validate_frame_needs,
02229:         )
02230:         # Raises MalformedPlanError on a malformed value/SHAPE; a valid-shape
02231:         # unknown jurisdiction + an empty evidence_needs both pass (non-fatal).
02232:         validate_frame_needs(research_frame)
02233: 
02234:     # ── Step 1: compile the effective query list ──────────────────────
02235:     # I-meta-005 Phase 4 (#988): `anchor_seed=False` (gap rounds) suppresses the
02236:     # broad `research_question` anchor on BOTH the prepend AND the scope-validator
02237:     # reinsertion, so a gap round fires ONLY the gap sub-queries (no wasted
02238:     # anchor re-run). Default True = OFF-mode byte-identical.
02239:     all_queries: list[str] = [research_question] if anchor_seed else []
02240:     if amplified_queries:
02241:         all_queries.extend(amplified_queries)
02242:     # Scope validation (de-drift)
02243:     if protocol:
02244:         valid = validate_amplified_queries(
02245:             all_queries, protocol, always_keep_anchor=anchor_seed,
02246:         )
02247:         effective_queries = valid.kept
02248:         notes.append(
02249:             f"scope_query_validator: {len(valid.kept)} kept / "
02250:             f"{len(valid.dropped)} dropped"
02251:         )
02252:     else:
02253:         effective_queries = list(all_queries)
02254: 
02255:     # ── Step 2: run Serper + S2 across queries ──────────────────────
02256:     seen_urls: set[str] = set()
02257:     candidates: list[SearchCandidate] = []
02258: 
02259:     # I-bug-776 (#817) layer-4 (Codex decision b): direct primary-trial DOI seed
02260:     # candidates. Injected at the FRONT so the fetch_cap slice always includes
02261:     # them (a reserved anchored-primary lane), and fetch_cap is bumped by the
02262:     # seed count below so they are ADDITIVE — they do not evict search/guideline
02263:     # candidates. They pass the SAME fetch / Unpaywall-OA / extraction / tier /

02272:                 query_origin="primary_trial_doi_seed",
02273:             ))
02274:             _n_seed_injected += 1

02280:

02282:     # seed_urls — no Serper/S2 fan-out and no domain backends. Used by the deepener pass so it fetches
02283:     # exactly the citation-snowball-discovered URLs (and nothing else) through the same chokepoint.

00050: def canonical_source_url(url: str) -> str:
00051:     """PUBLIC wrapper over `run_diff._normalize_url` (brief §2.1).
00052: 
00053:     Single dedup identity for the saturation novelty metric. Importing the
00054:     private `_normalize_url` directly is undesirable across modules, so this is
00055:     the public seam — it delegates verbatim (no reimplementation).
00056:     """
00057:     return _normalize_url(url or "")
00058: 
00059: 
00060: def _row_source_url(row: Any) -> str:
00061:     """Extract the row's canonical URL field (brief §2.1).
00062: 
00063:     Live rows carry `source_url` (NOT `url`), `live_retriever.py:2221`. Accepts
00064:     dict rows (the live shape) and falls back to object attributes defensively.
00065:     """
00066:     if isinstance(row, dict):
00067:         return row.get("source_url") or row.get("url") or ""
00068:     return getattr(row, "source_url", "") or getattr(row, "url", "") or ""

00071: def marginal_novelty(
00072:     prev_evidence_rows: list[Any],
00073:     new_round_rows: list[Any],
00074: ) -> float:
00075:     """Fraction of `new_round_rows` that are NOVEL vs `prev_evidence_rows`.
00076: 
00077:     Single dedup identity = canonical URL via `canonical_source_url`
00078:     (run_diff canonicalizer over `source_url`). A new row is NOVEL iff its
00079:     canonical URL is not already present in `prev_evidence_rows`. Intra-round
00080:     duplicates collapse too — two rows in the SAME new round with the same
00081:     canonical URL count as ONE novel (brief §2.1).
00082: 
00083:     Returns `len(novel) / max(1, len(new_round_rows))`.
00084:     """
00085:     prev_canon: set[str] = set()
00086:     for row in prev_evidence_rows or []:
00087:         canon = canonical_source_url(_row_source_url(row))
00088:         if canon:
00089:             prev_canon.add(canon)
00090: 
00091:     seen_this_round: set[str] = set()
00092:     novel = 0
00093:     for row in new_round_rows or []:
00094:         canon = canonical_source_url(_row_source_url(row))
00095:         # A row with no usable URL cannot be deduped — count it as novel once
00096:         # only if its (empty) canon hasn't been seen this round.
00097:         if canon in prev_canon or canon in seen_this_round:
00098:             continue
00099:         seen_this_round.add(canon)
00100:         novel += 1
00101:     return novel / max(1, len(new_round_rows or []))
00102:

codex
The envelope is booked in the parent before the isolated task, so the manifest/cap accounting is bounded by the envelope and precheck. 02205: def _partition_seeds(
02206:     sub_queries: list[str],
02207: ) -> tuple[list[str], list[str], list[str]]:
02208:     """Partition seed queries into web, academic, and exa buckets.
02209: 
02210:     Uses a simple heuristic: first 6 are web, next 2 are academic, last 1 is exa.
02211:     If fewer queries, distributes proportionally.
02212:     """
02213:     total = len(sub_queries)
02214:     if total == 0:
02215:         return [], [], []
02216: 
02217:     # Proportional split: ~67% web, ~22% academic, ~11% exa
02218:     web_count = max(1, int(total * 0.67))
02219:     acad_count = max(1, int(total * 0.22))
02220:     # Remaining go to exa (at least 0)
02221:     exa_count = max(0, total - web_count - acad_count)
02222: 
02223:     web_queries = sub_queries[:web_count]
02224:     academic_queries = sub_queries[web_count:web_count + acad_count]
02225:     exa_queries = sub_queries[web_count + acad_count:]
02226: 
02227:     return web_queries, academic_queries, exa_queries
02228: 
02229:

02239:         url = r.get(key, "")

 succeeded in 1090ms:
00001: """Pure, no-network question decomposition for the live retrieval path (I-meta-002-q1d #951 q1d-a).
00002: 
00003: The 5 golden benchmark questions are 40-70-word multi-clause paragraphs; four ship with NO
00004: hand-authored `amplified` query list, so the whole paragraph was fired as ~one keyword query and
00005: each sub-topic was under-retrieved (the Codex-verified S0 depth gap). This module decomposes the
00006: question into focused sub-queries deterministically — NO network, NO LLM, pure string operations —
00007: which the sweep prepends to the amplified-query list before `run_live_retrieval`.
00008: 
00009: Splitting is deliberately CONSERVATIVE (Codex brief-gate iter-1): split only on sentence terminators,
00010: semicolons, explicit enumerators, and top-level conjunction/connective boundaries — NEVER on bare
00011: commas. Conjunction / `versus` splits require BOTH sides to carry >= MIN_SPLIT_CONTENT_WORDS content
00012: words, so protected compounds ("safety and efficacy", "type 2 diabetes", "non-small cell lung cancer")
00013: are preserved BY CONSTRUCTION.
00014: """
00015: 
00016: from __future__ import annotations
00017: 
00018: import re
00019: 
00020: # Content-word tokenization (stopword-filtered, 3+ chars) — mirrors the lexical notion used by the
00021: # fetch-time rerank; pure, no model.
00022: _DECOMP_STOPWORDS = frozenset({
00023:     "the", "a", "an", "and", "or", "but", "is", "are", "was", "were", "of", "in", "on", "at",
00024:     "to", "for", "with", "by", "from", "as", "that", "this", "these", "those", "it", "its",
00025:     "be", "been", "what", "which", "who", "how", "why", "when", "where", "we", "our", "their",
00026:     "between", "into", "about", "than", "such", "does", "do", "can", "may", "any", "also",
00027: })
00028: 
00029: # Minimum content words for a sub-query to be KEPT (drop noise fragments).
00030: MIN_FRAGMENT_CONTENT_WORDS = 3
00031: # Minimum content words on EACH side of a conjunction/connective for the split to be allowed
00032: # (protects "safety and efficacy", "type 2 diabetes", etc. — each side has < 4 content words).
00033: MIN_SPLIT_CONTENT_WORDS = 4
00034: # Hard cap on emitted sub-queries (keeps the per-question query fan-out bounded; PR1's total
00035: # fetch_cap + rerank keep the corpus bounded regardless).
00036: DEFAULT_MAX_SUBQUERIES = 6
00037: 
00038: # Top-level connective boundaries we MAY split on (only when both sides are query-like).
00039: # "vs." is normalized to "vs" up front so it never reaches the terminator regex as a period.
00040: _CONNECTIVES = (" as well as ", " versus ", " vs ", " and ")
00041: # Protected "X and Y" clinical compounds: even when both surrounding fragments carry >=4 content
00042: # words, an `and` flanked by one of these (last-word-of-left, first-word-of-right) pairs is a single
00043: # concept, NOT a clause boundary (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1). Lowercased word pairs.
00044: _PROTECTED_AND_PAIRS = frozenset({
00045:     ("safety", "efficacy"), ("efficacy", "safety"),
00046:     ("signs", "symptoms"), ("symptoms", "signs"),
00047:     ("risks", "benefits"), ("benefits", "risks"),
00048:     ("morbidity", "mortality"), ("mortality", "morbidity"),
00049:     ("diagnosis", "treatment"), ("incidence", "prevalence"),
00050:     ("sensitivity", "specificity"), ("safety", "tolerability"),
00051: })
00052: # Additive connectives where a protected-compound guard applies ("safety and efficacy"). Comparators
00053: # (" versus ", " vs ") are NOT additive — "safety vs efficacy" is a valid split — so the guard skips them.
00054: _ADDITIVE_CONNECTIVES = (" and ", " as well as ")
00055: # Abbreviations whose internal period(s) must NOT be treated as sentence terminators. "vs." is
00056: # handled separately (normalized to "vs"). Periods here are masked (CASE-INSENSITIVELY, preserving
00057: # the original casing) before the terminator split.
00058: _ABBREVIATIONS = ("e.g.", "i.e.", "etc.", "et al.", "fig.", "no.", "approx.", "ca.")
00059: _ABBREVIATION_RE = re.compile("|".join(re.escape(a) for a in _ABBREVIATIONS), re.IGNORECASE)
00060: _PERIOD_MASK = "\x00"
00061: # Sentence/clause terminators we always split on. Enumerators like "1.", "2)", "(a)" are handled
00062: # by the terminator + enumerator regex below.
00063: _TERMINATOR_RE = re.compile(r"(?<=[.;?])\s+|\s*\|\s*")
00064: # Strip a leading enumerator marker ("1.", "2)", "(a)", "- ", "• ") from a clause.
00065: _ENUMERATOR_RE = re.compile(r"^\s*(?:\(?[0-9a-zA-Z]\)|[0-9]+[.)]|[-•])\s+")
00066: 
00067: 
00068: def _content_tokens(text: str) -> list[str]:
00069:     toks = re.findall(r"[A-Za-z][A-Za-z\-]{2,}", (text or "").lower())
00070:     return [t for t in toks if t not in _DECOMP_STOPWORDS]
00071: 
00072: 
00073: def _normalize(clause: str) -> str:
00074:     clause = _ENUMERATOR_RE.sub("", clause or "")
00075:     return re.sub(r"\s+", " ", clause).strip().strip(",;:")
00076: 
00077: 
00078: def _flanking_words(left: str, right: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
00079:     """The last word of `left` and the first word of `right`, lowercased + punctuation-stripped."""
00080:     lw = left.split()[-1].lower().strip(",;:.()") if left.split() else ""
00081:     rw = right.split()[0].lower().strip(",;:.()") if right.split() else ""
00082:     return lw, rw
00083: 
00084: 
00085: def _split_on_connectives(clause: str) -> list[str]:
00086:     """Split a clause on the FIRST top-level connective where both sides have
00087:     >= MIN_SPLIT_CONTENT_WORDS content words AND the connective is not flanked by a protected
00088:     clinical compound (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1); recurse on each side. Otherwise return [clause].
00089:     Bare commas / weak coordinators are never split points."""
00090:     lower = clause.lower()
00091:     for conn in _CONNECTIVES:
00092:         idx = lower.find(conn)
00093:         while idx != -1:
00094:             left = clause[:idx].strip()
00095:             right = clause[idx + len(conn):].strip()
00096:             protected = (
00097:                 conn in _ADDITIVE_CONNECTIVES
00098:                 and _flanking_words(left, right) in _PROTECTED_AND_PAIRS
00099:             )
00100:             if (len(_content_tokens(left)) >= MIN_SPLIT_CONTENT_WORDS
00101:                     and len(_content_tokens(right)) >= MIN_SPLIT_CONTENT_WORDS
00102:                     and not protected):
00103:                 return _split_on_connectives(left) + _split_on_connectives(right)
00104:             idx = lower.find(conn, idx + len(conn))
00105:     return [clause]
00106: 
00107: 
00108: def decompose_question(question: str, *, max_subqueries: int = DEFAULT_MAX_SUBQUERIES) -> list[str]:
00109:     """Decompose a multi-clause question into focused sub-query strings. Pure / no-network / no-LLM.
00110: 
00111:     Returns [] for a short single-clause question (the caller then falls back to today's behavior —
00112:     the full question is always seeded separately by `run_live_retrieval`). Sub-queries are normalized,
00113:     fragment-filtered (>= MIN_FRAGMENT_CONTENT_WORDS content words), de-duplicated case-insensitively,
00114:     and capped at `max_subqueries`, preserving leading-clause-first order.
00115:     """
00116:     if not question or not question.strip():
00117:         return []
00118:     # Stage 0: abbreviation protection (Codex diff-gate iter-1 P1). Normalize "vs." -> "vs" so the
00119:     # >=4-per-side connective guard handles comparators (never the period terminator), and MASK the
00120:     # internal periods of other abbreviations so they are not mistaken for sentence boundaries.
00121:     work = re.sub(r"\bvs\.", "vs", question, flags=re.IGNORECASE)
00122:     # Case-insensitive masking that PRESERVES the matched text's casing (so "E.g."/"Fig."/"No." at a
00123:     # sentence start are protected too — Codex diff-gate iter-2 P1).
00124:     work = _ABBREVIATION_RE.sub(lambda m: m.group(0).replace(".", _PERIOD_MASK), work)
00125:     # Stage 1: split on sentence terminators / enumerators / pipes.
00126:     primary = [c for c in _TERMINATOR_RE.split(work) if c and c.strip()]
00127:     # Stage 2: split each clause on safe top-level connectives.
00128:     clauses: list[str] = []
00129:     for clause in primary:
00130:         clauses.extend(_split_on_connectives(clause))
00131:     # Stage 3: unmask abbreviation periods, normalize, fragment-filter, dedup (case-insensitive), cap.
00132:     out: list[str] = []
00133:     seen: set[str] = set()
00134:     for clause in clauses:
00135:         norm = _normalize(clause.replace(_PERIOD_MASK, "."))
00136:         if len(_content_tokens(norm)) < MIN_FRAGMENT_CONTENT_WORDS:
00137:             continue
00138:         key = norm.lower()
00139:         if key in seen:
00140:             continue
00141:         seen.add(key)
00142:         out.append(norm)
00143:         if len(out) >= max_subqueries:
00144:             break
00145:     # A single clause out of a single-clause question adds nothing → fall back to [].
00146:     if len(out) <= 1:
00147:         return []
00148:     return out
